        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acsami.7b04407"><meta property="og:title" content="In Situ Grown Fe2O3 Single Crystallites on Reduced Graphene Oxide Nanosheets as High Performance Conversion Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/asset/images/acsami.7b04407.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="Electrochemical conversion reactions of metal oxides provide a new avenue to build high capacity anodes for sodium-ion batteries. However, the poor rate performance and cyclability of these conversion anodes remain a significant challenge for Na-ion battery applications because most of the conversion anodes suffer from sluggish kinetics and irreversible structural change during cycles. In this paper, we report an Fe2O3 single crystallites/reduced graphene oxide composite (Fe2O3/rGO), where the Fe2O3 single crystallites with a particle size of ∼300 nm were uniformly anchored on the rGO nanosheets, which provide a highly conductive framework to facilitate electron transport and a flexible matrix to buffer the volume change of the material during cycling. This Fe2O3/rGO composite anode shows a very high reversible capacity of 610 mAh g–1 at 50 mA g–1, a high Coulombic efficiency of 71% at the first cycle, and a strong cyclability with 82% capacity retention after 100 cycles, suggesting a potential feasibility for sodium-ion batteries. More significantly, the present work clearly illustrates that an electrochemical conversion anode can be made with high capacity utilization, strong rate capability, and stable cyclability through appropriately tailoring the lattice structure, particle size, and electronic conduction channels for a simple transition-metal oxide, thus offering abundant selections for development of low-cost and high-performance Na-storage electrodes."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/asset/images/acsami.7b04407.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/nwyw~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="90da8d1fa8b4b325-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da8d1fa8b4b325-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: '4060d9cd-f178-49f0-b3cc-589b692b4b91'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da8d1fa8b4b325-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'applied_materials_interfaces';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

Interfaces</i></span><span class="cit-fg-year"> 2017</span><span class="cit-fg-volume">, 9</span><span class="cit-fg-issue">, 23</span><span class="cit-fg-pageRange">, 19900-19907</span></span></span></div></div></div></div></div><input type="hidden" name="aamick" id="copyRights" value="/pb-assets/json/journal-info-1738791784303.json"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone5" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone5"><!-- Article Refresh Event Tracking -->
<script nonce="90da8d1fa8b4b325-SJC">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "aamick";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "In Situ Grown Fe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Single Crystallites on Reduced Graphene Oxide Nanosheets as High Performance Conversion Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b04407", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "In Situ Grown Fe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Single Crystallites on Reduced Graphene Oxide Nanosheets as High Performance Conversion Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b04407", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "In Situ Grown Fe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Single Crystallites on Reduced Graphene Oxide Nanosheets as High Performance Conversion Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b04407", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "In Situ Grown Fe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Single Crystallites on Reduced Graphene Oxide Nanosheets as High Performance Conversion Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b04407", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "In Situ Grown Fe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Single Crystallites on Reduced Graphene Oxide Nanosheets as High Performance Conversion Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b04407", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "In Situ Grown Fe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Single Crystallites on Reduced Graphene Oxide Nanosheets as High Performance Conversion Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b04407", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "In Situ Grown Fe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Single Crystallites on Reduced Graphene Oxide Nanosheets as High Performance Conversion Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b04407", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "In Situ Grown Fe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Single Crystallites on Reduced Graphene Oxide Nanosheets as High Performance Conversion Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b04407", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "In Situ Grown Fe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Single Crystallites on Reduced Graphene Oxide Nanosheets as High Performance Conversion Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b04407", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});

Tel: 86-027-68754526 (H.Y.).</div></div></div><div class="article_header-footer"><div class="article_header-footer-left"><div class="article_header-links"><input class="pub-doi" type="hidden" name="pub-doi" value="10.1021/acsami.7b04407"><a href="/doi/epdf/10.1021/acsami.7b04407?ref=article_openPDF" title="PDF" target="_blank" class="article__btn__secondary" data-id="article_header_OpenPDF"><i class="icon-open-pdf"></i><span>Open PDF</span></a><a href="#_i9" title="Supporting Information" class="article__btn__secondary internalNav" data-id="article_header_SupportingInfo"><i class="icon-supporting-info"></i><span>Supporting Information (1)</span></a><a href="/servlet/linkout?suffix=s0&amp;dbid=16384&amp;doi=10.1021/acsami.7b04407&amp;type=refOpenUrl&amp;url=http%3A%2F%2Fimp-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com%2Fopenurl%2F44IMP%2FICL_VU1%3Fid%3Ddoi%3A10.1021%252Facsami.7b04407%26sid%3Dliteratum%253Aachs%26pmid%3D28537405%26genre%3Darticle%26aulast%3DLi%26date%3D2017%26atitle%3DIn%2BSitu%2BGrown%2BFe2O3%2BSingle%2BCrystallites%2Bon%2BReduced%2BGraphene%2BOxide%2BNanosheets%2Bas%2BHigh%2BPerformance%2BConversion%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26jtitle%3DACS%2BApplied%2BMaterials%2B%2526%2BInterfaces%26title%3DACS%2BApplied%2BMaterials%2B%2526%2BInterfaces%26volume%3D9%26issue%3D23%26spage%3D19900%26epage%3D19907%26issn%3D1944-8244" title="OpenURL IMPERIAL COLLEGE LONDON" class="issue-item_open-url sfxLink"><img src="/userimages/9157ccea-6c85-4e5f-ac2a-6a9fd9422c17/sfxbutton-180e067c810" alt="OpenURL IMPERIAL COLLEGE LONDON"></a></div></div></div><div class="article_header-meta"><div class="article_header-meta-left"><input type="hidden" name="journalCodeForjhpLink" value="aamick"><input type="hidden" name="journalNameForjhpLink" value="ACS Applied Materials &amp; class="articleHeaderDropzone4" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone4"><div class="articleRightsPermissionsLink"><a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D19900%26pageCount%3D8%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DTing%2BLi%252C%2BAiqiong%2BQin%252C%2BLanlan%2BYang%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D9%26issueNum%3D23%26contentID%3Dacsami.7b04407%26title%3DIn%2BSitu%2BGrown%2BFe2O3%2BSingle%2BCrystallites%2Bon%2BReduced%2BGraphene%2BOxide%2BNanosheets%2Bas%2BHigh%2BPerformance%2BConversion%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26numPages%3D8%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D19907%26publicationDate%3DJune%2B2017" data-id="article_rights_permissions">Request reuse permissions</a></div></div></div></div></div><div class="article_header-metrics-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="article_header-metrics-dropzone"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="f_tgr1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/asset/images/medium/am-2017-04407u_0008.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/asset/images/large/am-2017-04407u_0008.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b04407&amp;id=f_tgr1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">Electrochemical conversion reactions of metal oxides provide a new avenue to build high capacity anodes for sodium-ion batteries. However, the poor rate performance and cyclability of these conversion anodes remain a significant challenge for Na-ion battery applications because most of the conversion anodes suffer from sluggish kinetics and irreversible structural change during cycles. In this paper, we report an Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> single crystallites/reduced graphene oxide composite (Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO), where the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> single crystallites with a particle size of ∼300 nm were uniformly anchored on the rGO nanosheets, which provide a highly conductive framework to facilitate electron transport and a flexible matrix to buffer the volume change of the material during cycling. This Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composite anode shows a very high reversible capacity of 610 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 50 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, a high Coulombic efficiency of 71% at the first cycle, and a strong cyclability with 82% capacity retention after 100 cycles, suggesting a potential feasibility for sodium-ion batteries. More significantly, the present work clearly illustrates that an electrochemical conversion anode can be made with high capacity utilization, strong rate capability, and stable cyclability through appropriately tailoring the lattice structure, particle size, and electronic conduction channels for a simple transition-metal oxide, thus offering abundant selections for development of low-cost and high-performance Na-storage electrodes.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D19900%26pageCount%3D8%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DTing%2BLi%252C%2BAiqiong%2BQin%252C%2BLanlan%2BYang%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D9%26issueNum%3D23%26contentID%3Dacsami.7b04407%26title%3DIn%2BSitu%2BGrown%2BFe2O3%2BSingle%2BCrystallites%2Bon%2BReduced%2BGraphene%2BOxide%2BNanosheets%2Bas%2BHigh%2BPerformance%2BConversion%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26numPages%3D8%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D19907%26publicationDate%3DJune%2B2017" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2017 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291517&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Batteries" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Batteries" class="article__tags__link">Batteries</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291331&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Composites" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Composites" class="article__tags__link">Composites</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291880&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Crystal structure" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Crystal%20structure" class="article__tags__link">Crystal structure</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291371&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrodes" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Electrodes" article__tags--keywords hlFld-Abstract"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Fe2o3+Single+Crystal&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_Fe2O3%20single%20crystal">Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> single crystal</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Reduced+Graphene+Oxide+Nanosheets&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_reduced%20graphene%20oxide%20nanosheets">reduced graphene oxide nanosheets</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Conversion+Anode&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_conversion%20anode">conversion anode</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Metal+Oxide&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_metal%20oxide">metal oxide</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Sodium-ion+Batteries&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_sodium-ion%20batteries">sodium-ion batteries</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i1">1 Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">Large-scale energy storage technologies are greatly needed to effectively utilize renewable electricity such as solar panels and wind farms for mobile transportation and smart grids. In the pursuit of these technologies, many new types of electrochemical batteries have been proposed for future electric vehicle and distributed electric storage applications. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1 ref2'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2" aria-label="reference 1 and 2">(1, 2)</a> Among all the new battery chemistries being developed, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered to be one of the most attractive candidates because of their similar intercalation chemistry to Li-ion batteries and natural abundance of sodium resources. However, finding suitable Na-host materials for battery application is difficult because the larger sized Na<sup>+</sup> ions are frustrated to move freely in the rigid oxide lattices. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3 ref4 ref5'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref3 ref4 ref5" aria-label="reference 3 to 5">(3-5)</a> Up to date, only a few of Na-intercalation anodes are found to have acceptable redox capacity and certain cyclability. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6 ref7 ref8 ref9 ref10'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref6 ref7 ref8 ref9 ref10" aria-label="reference 6 to 10">(6-10)</a> To overcome this difficult circumstance, several types of Na-alloying compounds are developed to demonstrate remarkable high Na-storage capacities, such as Na<sub>3.75</sub>Sn (847 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>), <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11 ref12'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref11 ref12" aria-label="reference 11 and 12">(11, 12)</a> Na<sub>3</sub>Sb (660 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>), <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13 ref14'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref13 ref14" aria-label="reference 13 and 14">(13, 14)</a> and Na<sub>3</sub>P (2560 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15 ref16'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref15 ref16" aria-label="reference 15 and 16">(15, 16)</a> However, the huge volume changes of these host materials during alloying/dealloying reactions lead to a structural instability, which severely hinders their applications for Na-ion batteries. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9 ref17'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref9 ref17" aria-label="reference 9 and 17">(9, 17)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">Electrochemical conversion reaction provides a new mechanism to realize high Na-storage capacity through reversible structural conversion to utilize the multioxidation states of transition-metal elements. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18 ref19'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18 ref19" aria-label="reference 18 and 19">(18, 19)</a> In recent years, many types of metal oxides, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20 ref21 ref22 ref23 ref24'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref20 ref21 ref22 ref23 ref24" aria-label="reference 20 to 24">(20-24)</a> metal sulfides, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25 ref26'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref25 ref26" aria-label="reference 25 and 26">(25, 26)</a> metal selenides, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27 ref28'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref27 ref28" aria-label="reference 27 and 28">(27, 28)</a> metal nitrides, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref29" aria-label="reference 29">(29)</a> and metal phosphides <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30 ref31'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30 ref31" aria-label="reference 30 and 31">(30, 31)</a> have been reported for Na-storage anodes. Among them, Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> seems to be particularly attractive, owing to its natural abundance, environmental benignity, and high theoretical capacity (1007 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32 ref33 ref34 ref35 ref36 ref37 ref38 ref39 ref40'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32 ref33 ref34 ref35 ref36 ref37 ref38 ref39 ref40" aria-label="reference 32 to 40">(32-40)</a> However, most of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> electrodes reported so far suffer from low utilization, inferior cycling performance, and poor rate capability, due to their low electron conductivity and large specific volume change during the electrochemical conversion processes. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32 ref37'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32 ref37" aria-label="reference 32 and 37">(32, 37)</a> To overcome these problems, many efforts are devoted to tailor the nanostructure of Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34 ref35 ref36 ref37'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref34 ref35 ref36 ref37" aria-label="reference 34 to 37">(34-37)</a> or to coat Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> nanoparticles with conductive carbon. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32 ref37 ref38 ref39 ref40'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32 ref37 ref38 ref39 ref40" aria-label="reference 32 and 37 to 40">(32, 37-40)</a> For example, Zhou’s group reported graphene-supported Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> nanocrystals with excellent cycling performance and rate capability. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32" aria-label="reference 32">(32)</a> Chen’s group synthesized a 3D porous γ-Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C nanocomposite, which provides a capacity of about 400 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> with a high cycling stability over 200 cycles. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref37" aria-label="reference 37">(37)</a> Such nanoarchitectures can indeed enhance the kinetics and performance of Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> conversion materials.</div><div class="NLM_p">From the thermodynamic point of view, nanosized particles are intrinsically unstable because of their high surface energy, and easy agglomeration during electrochemical cycling is inevitable. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41 ref42'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref41 ref42" aria-label="reference 41 and 42">(41, 42)</a> Such an effect becomes even prominent with downsizing the nanoparticles and eventually leads to an unavoidable capacity fading if no special strategy is introduced. On the other hand, the large surface area of nanoparticles causes a high irreversible capacity during the solid electrolyte interface (SEI) formation and results in a low Coulombic efficiency at initial cycles. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref41" aria-label="reference 41">(41)</a> As an anode material, the low Coulombic efficiency will bring a significant capacity loss at the initial cycle for the batteries. More significantly, such a capacity loss is even larger for SIBs than for Li-ion batteries, as it is revealed that the overall SEI coverage on the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> electrode is more prominent in the Na-half batteries than in those based on Li-half batteries. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33 ref43'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref33 ref43" aria-label="reference 33 and 43">(33, 43)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">Very recently, it was reported that single-crystal metal oxides such as Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, CuO, and V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub> show excellent electrochemical performance with high Li- or Na-storage capacity and satisfactory cyclability. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44 ref45 ref46 ref47'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref44 ref45 ref46 ref47" aria-label="reference 44 to 47">(44-47)</a> It was found that the predominantly exposed facets of the single crystals have relatively high surface energy, thus providing active sites for accommodating lithium or sodium ions and then for a fast conversion reaction. Furthermore, it was also observed that, although they suffered from the structural transformation of the electrode material during lithiation/delithiation processes, the conversion products can inherit the crystallographic orientation of single-crystal α-Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref48" aria-label="reference 48">(48)</a> These results suggest that single-crystal structure may have a strong resistance to the aggregation of nanoparticles and a strong tendency to keep the electrode structure reversibly changed, thus ensuring the cycling stability.</div><div class="NLM_p last">In the present work, we synthesized monocrystalline Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> particles with a diameter of hundreds of nanometers, which are uniformly anchored onto reduced graphene oxide nanosheets (rGO) through a one-step solvothermal method, and investigated the electrochemical performance, especially cycling stability of the material. Due to the structural integrity and appropriate size of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> single crystallites along with the abundant 3D electron transport channels provided by rGO sheets, this Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composite anode shows a very high reversible capacity of 610 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 50 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, a high Coulombic efficiency of 71% at the first cycle, and a strong cyclability (82% capacity retention over 100 cycles), suggesting a potential feasibility to use this conversion anode for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">2 Experimental Section</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec2_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i3" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i3">2.1 Materials Synthesis</h3><div class="NLM_p last">Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composites were prepared by a one-step solvothermal process. In a typical synthesis, 10 mL of 0.4 mol L<sup>–1</sup> Fe(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub> methanol solution was mixed with 60 mL of 1 mg mL<sup>–1</sup> GO (Graphene Oxide, 99% purity, Nanjing XFNANO Materials Tech Co., Ltd., Nanjing, China) methanol dispersion under vigorous stirring and ultrasonic surging for 1 h. After dropwise addition of 14 mL of aqueous ammonia and stirring for 0.5 h, the formed homogeneous mixture was added into a 100 mL Teflon-lined stainless steel autoclave at 180 °C for about 10 h. When cooling down to room temperature, the solid product was centrifuged and washed with distilled water and ethanol, and then dried at 60 °C under vacuum. Pure Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> and rGO samples were synthesized using the above-mentioned method in the absence of GO or Fe(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, respectively.</div></div><div id="sec2_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i4" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i4">2.2 Structural Characterizations</h3><div class="NLM_p">The crystalline structural features of the as-prepared samples were characterized by X-ray diffraction (XRD, Bruker, D8-advance, Cu Kα radiation). The morphologies of Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> monocrystals and as-prepared composite were observed using scanning electron microscopy (SEM, FEI Quanta-200) and transmission electron microscope (TEM, JEOL, JEM-2100FEF). The structures of the GO and rGO in Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composite were investigated by confocal Raman microspectroscopy (Renishaw, RM-1000, 514.5 nm excitation). The content of the rGO in the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composite was obtained by thermogravimetric analysis (TGA, TA, Q500) in air from room temperature to 800 °C at a heating rate of 10 °C min<sup>–1</sup>. X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) was conducted on a VG Multilab 2000 spectrometer. Binding energies were calibrated by setting the C 1s hydrocarbon component peak at 284.6 eV.</div><div class="NLM_p last">To characterize the structural changes during cycling, ex situ XRD and XPS analysis are conducted for the electrode samples, which are taken out from the cycled cells at different depths of charge and discharge (0.01–3.0 V), and rinsed with dimethyl carbonate solvent in an Ar-filled glovebox.</div></div><div id="sec2_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i5" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i5">2.3 Electrochemical Measurements</h3><div class="NLM_p last">Electrochemical performances of the electrode materials were examined by coin cells. The electrodes were fabricated by coating a slurry, which was composed of 80 wt % materials, 10 wt % CMC binder, and 10 wt % Super P, onto a copper foil and drying at 60 °C overnight under vacuum. The mass loading of the active material within the film is about 2.5 mg cm<sup>–2</sup>. Coin cells (2032 type) were assembled in an argon-filled glovebox using the as-prepared electrode as a working electrode, a sodium metal disk as the counter and reference electrode, and a microporous membrane (Celgard 2400) as the separator. The electrolyte used is prepared by dissolving NaPF<sub>6</sub> (1 M) in the solvent of ethylene carbonate (EC)/diethyl carbonate (DEC) (1:1 by volume) with 5% fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC). The galvanostatic discharge/charge measurement was carried out using a LAND cycler (Wuhan Kingnuo Electronic Co., China). The charge/discharge specific capacity of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrode is calculated based on the mass of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composite. Cyclic voltammetry was conducted using coin cells on an electrochemical workstation (CHI 660e, Chenhua Instruments Co., China) at a scan rate of 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. Electrochemical impedance spectra (EIS) were obtained on an IM 6e impedance measuring unit (Zahner) with an AC voltage of 5 mV amplitude from 100 kHz to100 mHz.</div></div></div><div id="sec3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i6">3 Results and Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">The Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO nanocomposite was synthesized by a simple one-step solvothermal process. As shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig1" aria-label="Figure 1">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>, GO methanol dispersion was first mixed with Fe(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub> under vigorous stirring to form a precursor solution, in which Fe<sup>3+</sup> cations were adsorbed uniformly on GO platelets through electrostatic interaction of oxygen-containing functional groups such as hydroxyl, carboxyl, and epoxyl. Then, Fe(OH)<sub>3</sub> crystals were in situ produced and anchored onto the GO nanosheets after the intervention of aqueous ammonia. During the subsequent solvothermal treatment, GO was converted to rGO with the reduction of methanol and Fe(OH)<sub>3</sub> decomposed to form Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> nanocrystals simultaneously.</div><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/asset/images/medium/am-2017-04407u_0001.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/asset/images/large/am-2017-04407u_0001.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. Schematic illustration of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composite formation process.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/asset/images/large/am-2017-04407u_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b04407&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">The structure and morphology of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composites were characterized by XRD, Raman, TGA, SEM, and TEM measurements. As shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig2" aria-label="Figure 2">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>a, both the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composite and the pure Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> sample show strong XRD signals that can all be indexed to α-Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> (JCPDS No. 33-0664), suggesting high purity and crystallinity of the as-synthesized Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> particles. The reduction of GO and its content in the composite were confirmed by Raman spectra and TGA, respectively. <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig2" aria-label="Figure 2">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>b gives the Raman spectra of the pristine GO sample and Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composite. The two Raman bands observed at about 1355 and 1605 cm<sup>–1</sup> in both cases are characterized as D-band and G-band, respectively, due to characteristic Raman shifts of graphite. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref49" aria-label="reference 49">(49)</a> It is obvious that the intensity ratio for the D-band to G-band (<i>I</i><sub>D</sub>/<i>I</i><sub>G</sub>) of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composite is higher than that of GO, indicative of the certain reduction of GO in the solvothermal treatment. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50 ref51'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref50 ref51" aria-label="reference 50 and 51">(50, 51)</a> As estimated by TGA in air (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig2" aria-label="Figure 2">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>c), the content of rGO in the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composite was determined to be 15.7%, in good accordance with the theoretical value (15.79%).</div><figure id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/asset/images/medium/am-2017-04407u_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/asset/images/large/am-2017-04407u_0002.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. (a) XRD patterns of pure Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composite, and rGO sample. (b) Raman spectra of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composite and GO sample. (c) TGA curve of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composite.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/asset/images/large/am-2017-04407u_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b04407&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">The morphology and microstructure of pure Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> and the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composite were observed via SEM and TEM spectrometry. As seen in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>a (SEM), the pure Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> particles are homogeneously distributed with a uniform size. It is further confirmed by the TEM image (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>c) that the single Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> crystallite displays a rhombic structure with a diameter of ∼300 nm. On the other hand, for the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composite, it is clearly observed that the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> particles are anchored tightly on the rGO sheets (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>b, SEM) and the monodisperse Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> particles are uniformly wrapped in graphene sheets (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>d, TEM). The high-resolution TEM image of <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>e indicates a single Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> crystallite in the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composite with a particle size of about 300 nm, which is similar to that of the pure Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> sample. <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>f displays the corresponding selected area electron diffraction pattern (SAED) from the above single crystallite. It shows a set of clear diffraction spots, all of which can be well indexed as (104), (110), and (012) planes of pure α-Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> phase. The results above confirmed that single-crystal Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> particles with a diameter of ∼300 nm were synthesized in both the samples of pure Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> and Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composite (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>f and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/suppl_file/am7b04407_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S-1</a>), and the particle size (∼300 nm) is significantly larger than those of previously reported nanosized Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32 ref33 ref34 ref37 ref39 ref40'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32 ref33 ref34 ref37 ref39 ref40" aria-label="reference 32 to 34, 37, 39 and 40">(32-34, 37, 39, 40)</a></div><figure id="fig3" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/asset/images/medium/am-2017-04407u_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/asset/images/large/am-2017-04407u_0003.jpeg" id="gr3" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. (a) SEM image of pure Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> sample. (b) SEM image of Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO nanocomposite. (c) TEM image of pure Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> sample. (d) TEM image of Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO nanocomposite. (e) TEM image of a single crystal of Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO nanocomposite at high magnification. (f) The corresponding SAED pattern from (e).</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/asset/images/large/am-2017-04407u_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b04407&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">The electrochemical conversion performances of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrode were evaluated by cyclic voltammetry (CV) and galvanostatic discharge–charge measurements. <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig4" aria-label="Figure 4">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>a shows typical CV curves of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrode at a scan rate of 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup> within the voltage range of 0.01–3.0 V. During the first negative scan, two broad cathodic peaks appeared at 1.1 and 0.5 V, respectively, which is different from the subsequent cycles, suggesting the irreversible formation of a solid electrolyte interface (SEI) layer in the initial sodiation reaction for the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrode. At subsequent scans, two cathodic peaks emerged at 0.7 and 1.1 V, following two anodic peaks at 0.8 and 0.4 V, respectively, which are reasonably originated from the reversible redox reactions of Fe<sup>3+</sup> ↔ Fe<sup>2+</sup> and Fe<sup>2+</sup> ↔ Fe<sup>0</sup> couples. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33 ref34 ref37'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref33 ref34 ref37" aria-label="reference 33, 34 and 37">(33, 34, 37)</a></div><figure id="fig4" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/asset/images/medium/am-2017-04407u_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/asset/images/large/am-2017-04407u_0004.jpeg" id="gr4" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. (a) CV curves of Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrode at a scan rate of 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup> between 0.01 and 3.00 V. (b) Charge/discharge curves of Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrode in the voltage range of 0.01–3.00 V at 50 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. (c) Cycling curves of Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> and Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrodes at 50 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. (d) Rate performance of Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> and Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrodes at different current densities.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/asset/images/large/am-2017-04407u_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b04407&amp;id=fig4"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p"><a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig4" aria-label="Figure 4">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>b provides the discharge/charge profiles of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrode in the voltage range of 0.01–3.0 V at a current density of 50 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. In good agreement with its CV features, the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrode displayed sloping discharge/charge profiles with broad voltage plateaus at 0.8–0.4 V and 0.7–1.1 V, respectively, suggesting the reversible conversion reactions of Na<sup>+</sup> with the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> crystallite. The Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrode showed initial discharge/charge capacities of 861 and 611 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> (calculated based on the mass of Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composite), resulting in a Coulombic efficiency of 71% at the first cycle, which is relatively higher than those of the previously reported nanoscaled Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32 ref37 ref39 ref40'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32 ref37 ref39 ref40" aria-label="reference 32, 37, 39 and 40">(32, 37, 39, 40)</a> This is attributed to the relatively larger size (∼300 nm) and, therefore, lower surface area of these Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> particles, which reduce the irreversible capacity consumed for the formation of the SEI film and elevate the initial Coulombic efficiency. After the following cycles, the reversible capacity maintained stable at ∼610 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>. Upon the subtraction of specific capacity of rGO (50 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/suppl_file/am7b04407_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S-4 and S-5</a>), the reversible conversion capacity of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> crystallites in the electrode is determined to be about 723 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>, corresponding to 4.3 Na<sup>+</sup> conversion with per Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> unit.</div><div class="NLM_p">The cycling performances of pure Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> and Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composite electrodes were comparatively evaluated to reveal the electrochemical enhancement of the graphene matrix for the conversion reactions. As seen in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig4" aria-label="Figure 4">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>c, the pristine Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> electrode exhibited a Na-storage capacity of 330 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> in the initial cycle and maintained a reversible capacity of 235 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 100 cycles, corresponding to a capacity retention rate of 71.2%. Meanwhile, the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composite electrode delivered a much higher reversible capacity of ∼500 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 100 cycles with a capacity retention rate of 81.8%. Both of the pure Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> and Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrodes show a satisfactory cyclability. In comparison with the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> nanoparticles previously reported, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32 ref37 ref38 ref39'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32 ref37 ref38 ref39" aria-label="reference 32 and 37 to 39">(32, 37-39)</a> the as-prepared Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> single nanocrystals did not show a fast capacity fading but a much stable cyclability even when they were used directly in its pristine form, demonstrating that the single-crystal structure of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> particles is beneficial to maintain the structural integrity of the electrode and the electrochemical reversibility for the conversion processes.</div><div class="NLM_p">Sluggish kinetics has been a severe issue for battery application of conversion electrodes. However, the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> single crystallites demonstrate a strong rate capability, i.e., fast structural conversion during charge/discharge processes. <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig4" aria-label="Figure 4">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>d shows the rate performance of pristine Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> and Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrodes cycled at different current densities from 50 to 2000 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. The Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrode delivered a reversible capacity of 216 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at a high current density of 2000 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, and recovered 95% of its original capacity (∼500 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>) when the current density was returned to 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. In contrast, the pure Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> electrode only showed 54 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at a high current density of 2000 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. The greatly enhanced rate capability of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composite is obviously attributed to the existence of the rGO nanosheets, which act as a highly conductive and flexible buffering matrix to facilitate the electron conduction and alleviate the structural change of the electrode during the conversion reactions.</div><div class="NLM_p">Electrochemical impedance spectra (EIS) of Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> and Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composite electrodes were measured at different cycles to further confirm the electrochemical enhancement of rGO on the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrode (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig5" aria-label="Figure 5">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>). The fitted impedance parameters on the basis of the equivalent circuit inset (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig5" aria-label="Figure 5">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>a,b) are listed in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#tbl1" aria-label="Table 1">Table </a><a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">1</a>. It is observed that charge transfer resistance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>) of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> electrode was 441 Ω at the 1st cycle and increased to 3470 Ω at the 40th cycle. In contrast, the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrode is 80.2 and 777.1 Ω at the 1st and 40th cycles, respectively, suggesting that the rGO carbon matrix offers a well-connected electron transport network which significantly accelerates the electronic conduction during the conversion reaction as well as enhance the rate capability of the composite electrode.</div><figure id="fig5" data-index="5" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 5</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/asset/images/medium/am-2017-04407u_0005.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/asset/images/large/am-2017-04407u_0005.jpeg" id="gr5" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 5. Electrochemical impedance spectra (EIS) of Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> (a) and Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO (b) electrodes at charge state after 1st and 40th cycles. The equivalent circuits are given as the inset.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/asset/images/large/am-2017-04407u_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b04407&amp;id=fig5"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_table-wrap" id="tbl1"><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption"><div class="NLM_caption" id=""><div class="title2">Table 1. Results of the EIS Simulation Based on the Equivalent Circuit<a class="ref internalNav" href="#t1fn1" aria-label="a"><sup>a</sup></a></div></div></div><div class="scrollable-table-wrap"><table class="table" border="0"><colgroup><col align="left"><col align="char" char="."><col align="char" char="."><col align="char" char="."><col align="char" char="."></colgroup><thead><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center">&nbsp;</th><th class="rowsep1 colsep0" colspan="2" scope="col" align="center" char=".">Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub></th><th
