align="center">cycle</th><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center" char="."><i>R</i><sub>SEI</sub> (Ω)</th><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center" char="."><i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> (Ω)</th><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center" char="."><i>R</i><sub>SEI</sub> (Ω)</th><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center" char="."><i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> (Ω)</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">1st&nbsp;cycle</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">17.9</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">441</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">5.7</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">80.2</td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">40th&nbsp;cycle</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">76.5</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">3470</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">7.1</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">777.1</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="NLM_table-wrap-foot" id="IDtable-wrap-foot-t1fn1"><div class="footnote" id="t1fn1"><sup>a</sup><p class="last"><i>R</i><sub>SEI</sub> and <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> are the resistances of SEI film and charge transfer, respectively.</p></div></div></div><div class="NLM_p">The structural conversion mechanism can be visualized from ex situ XRD and XPS characterizations of the cycled Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrode at different charge/discharge states. As seen in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig6" aria-label="Figure 6">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>a, the as-prepared electrode shows a clear XRD pattern of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> lattice. After discharged to 0.6 V, the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> signals almost disappeared, while the main reflection of metal Fe at 20.3° (JCPDS No. 01-1267) was observed. Upon a fully discharged of the electrode to 0.01 V, the XRD signal of Fe became stronger; meanwhile, the XRD peaks characteristic of Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> vanished completely, implying that the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> crystallites had entirely transformed into metallic Fe through the electrochemical conversion reaction. The traceable XRD signal from the Na<sub>2</sub>O phase is invisible, possibly due to the poor diffractions of nanosized Na<sub>2</sub>O produced by conversion reaction. In the reversed charge process, the peak intensity of the Fe phase decreased and completely disappeared at a fully charged state of 3.0 V, while a weak peak of Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> reappeared, indicating a high reversibility of the structural change during the discharge/charge process. This reversible conversion mechanism has also been confirmed by ex situ XPS analysis of Fe element in the cycled Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrode at different oxidation states. As shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig6" aria-label="Figure 6">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>b, the pristine Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrode gives two XPS peaks at 710.7 and 724.3 eV, which are attributed to the binding energies of Fe<sup>3+</sup> 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and Fe<sup>3+</sup> 2p<sub>1/2</sub>, respectively. Once discharged to 0.01 V, the above-mentioned binding energy peaks vanished and new imperceptible peaks at 706.8 and 720 eV appeared, corresponding to the binding energies of Fe<sup>0</sup> 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and Fe<sup>0</sup> 2p<sub>1/2</sub>, respectively, indicative of the reduction of all the Fe<sup>3+</sup> ions in the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> lattice to Fe<sup>0</sup>. The binding energies returned to the original values when it recharged to 3.0 V, which suggests a reversible structural conversion of Fe<sup>0</sup> to Fe<sup>3+</sup> ions in the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> crystallite. The above-mentioned XPS and XRD results evidently demonstrate the reversible structural conversion of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> with Na<sup>+</sup> during discharge–charge cycles.</div><figure id="fig6" data-index="6" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 6</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/asset/images/medium/am-2017-04407u_0006.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/asset/images/large/am-2017-04407u_0006.jpeg" id="gr6" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 6. (a) Ex situ XRD patterns of Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrodes at different discharge and charge states as labeled in the figure. (b) Ex situ XPS survey of Fe 2p spectra for Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrodes at various discharge and charge states as labeled in the figure.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/asset/images/large/am-2017-04407u_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b04407&amp;id=fig6"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">TEM images of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrode after 100 cycles were observed to evidence the structural stability of the electrode enduring long-term discharge and charge. Compared with the original morphology (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>d,e), the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> crystallites in the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrode (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig7" aria-label="Figure 7">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>a,b) still maintain the single-crystal structure without any cracks or aggregations after 100 cycles. The HRTEM image (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig7" aria-label="Figure 7">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>c) of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrode at the fully discharged state shows the lattice fringe with a <i>d</i>-space of 0.201 nm, corresponding to the (110) planes of Fe. When the electrode is fully charged, the lattice fringe of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> (104) phase was observed (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig7" aria-label="Figure 7">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>d), which is in agreement with the results of ex situ XRD analysis. This outstanding structural stability of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrode arose from its single-crystal structure feature, which maintains the mechanical integrity of the electrode during cycling. Moreover, it is also speculated that the stable and conductive rGO carbon matrix wrapped on Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> nanograins can not only facilitate the electronic transports but also effectively accommodate the volume changes during the conversion process, resulting in a significantly improved cycling stability.</div><figure id="fig7" data-index="7" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 7</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/asset/images/medium/am-2017-04407u_0007.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/asset/images/large/am-2017-04407u_0007.jpeg" id="gr7" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 7. (a) TEM image of Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrode after 100 discharge/charge cycles at 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup>; (b) at higher magnification of image (a). (c) HRTEM image of Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrode at a fully discharged state. (d) HRTEM image of Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO electrode at a fully charged state.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b04407/asset/images/large/am-2017-04407u_0007.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b04407&amp;id=fig7"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div><div id="sec4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i8">4 Conclusions</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">In summary, a monocrystalline Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composite was prepared by a one-step solvothermal method, in which Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> single crystallites with a diameter of ∼300 nm were uniformly anchored onto an rGO nanosheet. The as-prepared Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/rGO composite exhibits a high reversible Na-storage capacity of 610 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 50 mA g<sup>–1</sup> with a high Coulombic efficiency of 71% at the first cycle, an outstanding rate capability with 216 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at a high current of 2000 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, and an excellent cycling stability with 82% capacity retention over 100 cycles. It is thought that the single-crystal structure of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> particles is favorable to prevent the aggregation of the nanograins during the cycling and enhance the cycling stability, and the relatively large particle size benefits to raise the high initial Coulombic efficiency. The rGO nanosheet provides a fast electron transport network, which improves the specific capacity and rate capability. The present work indicates that a high capacity utilization and high rate capability of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> nanocrystallites can be realized through electrochemical conversion reaction by tailoring the lattice structure, particle size, and building appropriate electronic conduction channels of the Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> nanocrystals.</div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div                         cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrical Energy Storage for the Grid: A Battery of Choices</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dunn, Bruce; Kamath, Haresh; Tarascon, Jean-Marie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Science (Washington, DC, United States)</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">334</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6058</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Association for the Advancement of Science</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The increasing interest in energy storage for the grid can be attributed to multiple factors, including the capital costs of managing peak demands, the investments needed for grid reliability, and the integration of renewable energy sources.  Although existing energy storage is dominated by pumped hydroelec., there is the recognition that battery systems can offer a no. of high-value opportunities, provided that lower costs can be obtained.  The battery systems reviewed here include sodium-sulfur batteries that are com. available for grid applications, redox-flow batteries that offer low cost, and lithium-ion batteries whose development for com. electronics and elec. vehicles is being applied to grid storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrZwDymuubZm7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liFdyA_624CAw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXhsVGktL%252FJ&amp;md5=5035bfda7631ad9d075e8836e61146ef</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit2" data-doi="10.1038/nchem.2085"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Larcher, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tarascon, J. M.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Towards Greener and More Sustainable Batteries for Electrical Energy Storage</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat. Chem.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">7</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">19</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">29</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/nchem.2085</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D7%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D19-29%26journal%3DNat.%2BChem.%26author%3DD.%2BLarcher%26author%3DJ.%2BM.%2BTarascon%26title%3DTowards%2BGreener%2Band%2BMore%2BSustainable%2BBatteries%2Bfor%2BElectrical%2BEnergy%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1038%252Fnchem.2085&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b04407&amp;doiOfLink=10.1038%2Fnchem.2085&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Towards greener and more sustainable batteries for electrical energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Larcher, D.; Tarascon, J.-M.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">19-29</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NCAHBB</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1755-4330</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Ever-growing energy needs and depleting fossil-fuel resources demand the pursuit of sustainable energy alternatives, including both renewable energy sources and sustainable storage technologies.  It is therefore essential to incorporate material abundance, eco-efficient synthetic processes and life-cycle anal. into the design of new electrochem. storage systems.  At present, a few existing technologies address these issues, but in each case, fundamental and technol. hurdles remain to be overcome.  Here the authors provide an overview of the current state of energy storage from a sustainability perspective.  The authors introduce the notion of sustainability through discussion of the energy and environmental costs of state-of-the-art Li-ion batteries, considering elemental abundance, toxicity, synthetic methods and scalability.  With the same themes in mind, the authors also highlight current and future electrochem. storage systems beyond Li-ion batteries.  The complexity and importance of recycling battery materials is also discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGph4-d2B3Q8DLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liWaqAYuhiRqg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvFKlsrjF&amp;md5=977f0fc171bb41af30457715fc0ded72</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201200026"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, S.                         cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrode materials for rechargeable sodium-ion batteries: potential alternatives to current lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Sung-Wook; Seo, Dong-Hwa; Ma, Xiaohua; Ceder, Gerbrand; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Lithium (Li)-ion batteries (LIB) have governed the current worldwide rechargeable battery market due to their outstanding energy and power capability.  In particular, the LIB's role in enabling elec. vehicles (EVs) has been highlighted to replace the current oil-driven vehicles in order to reduce the usage of oil resources and generation of CO2 gases.  Unlike Li, sodium is one of the more abundant elements on Earth and exhibits similar chem. properties to Li, indicating that Na chem. could be applied to a similar battery system.  In the 1970s-80s, both Na-ion and Li-ion electrodes were investigated, but the higher energy d. of Li-ion cells made them more applicable to small, portable electronic devices, and research efforts for rechargeable batteries have been mainly concd. on LIB since then.  Recently, research interest in Na-ion batteries (NIB) has been resurrected, driven by new applications with requirements different from those in portable electronics, and to address the concern on Li abundance.  In this article, both neg. and pos. electrode materials in NIB are briefly reviewed.  While the voltage is generally lower and the vol. change upon Na removal or insertion is larger for Na-intercalation electrodes, compared to their Li equiv., the power capability can vary depending on the crystal structures.  It is concluded that cost-effective NIB can partially replace LIB, but requires further investigation and improvement.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGonnrfiSUpaRrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liWaqAYuhiRqg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhtVOrtLjF&amp;md5=485b20393bb8876b2f69ca708aeba606</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1039/c2ee02781j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Palomares, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Serras, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Villaluenga, I.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hueso, K.                         cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-ion batteries, recent advances and present challenges to become low cost energy storage systems</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Palomares, Veronica; Serras, Paula; Villaluenga, Irune; Hueso, Karina B.; Carretero-Gonzalez, Javier; Rojo, Teofilo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Energy prodn. and storage have become key issues concerning our welfare in daily life.  Present challenges for batteries are twofold.  In the first place, the increasing demand for powering systems of portable electronic devices and zero-emission vehicles stimulates research towards high energy and high voltage systems.  In the second place, low cost batteries are required in order to advance towards smart elec. grids that integrate discontinuous energy flow from renewable sources, optimizing the performance of clean energy sources.  Na-ion batteries can be the key for the second point, because of the huge availability of sodium, its low price and the similarity of both Li and Na insertion chemistries.  In spite of the lower energy d. and voltage of Na-ion based technologies, they can be focused on applications where the wt. and footprint requirement is less drastic, such as elec. grid storage.  Much work has to be done in the field of Na-ion in order to catch up with Li-ion technol.  Cathodic and anodic materials must be optimized, and new electrolytes will be the key point for Na-ion success.  This review will gather the up-to-date knowledge about Na-ion battery materials, with the aim of providing a wide view of the systems that have already been explored and a starting point for the new research on this battery technol.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoRYtxfVVW_sLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liWaqAYuhiRqg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XivFWnu7s%253D&amp;md5=72869139086b8ee9adec746418ff84b1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1039/c3ee40811f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hong, S.                         cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Charge carriers in rechargeable batteries: Na ions vs. Li ions</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hong, Sung You; Kim, Youngjin; Park, Yuwon; Choi, Aram; Choi, Nam-Soon; Lee, Kyu Tae</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  We discuss the similarities and dissimilarities of sodium- and lithium-ion batteries in terms of neg. and pos. electrodes.  Compared to the comprehensive body of work on lithium-ion batteries, research on sodium-ion batteries is still at the germination stage.  Since both sodium and lithium are alkali metals, they share similar chem. properties including ionicity, electronegativity and electrochem. reactivity.  They accordingly have comparable synthetic protocols and electrochem. performances, which indicates that sodium-ion batteries can be successfully developed based on previously applied approaches or methods in the lithium counterpart.  The electrode materials in Li-ion batteries provide the best library for research on Na-ion batteries because many Na-ion insertion hosts have their roots in Li-ion insertion hosts.  However, the larger size and different bonding characteristics of sodium ions influence the thermodn. and/or kinetic properties of sodium-ion batteries, which leads to unexpected behavior in electrochem. performance and reaction mechanism, compared to lithium-ion batteries.  This perspective provides a comparative overview of the major developments in the area of pos. and neg. electrode materials in both Li-ion and Na-ion batteries in the past decade.  Highlighted are concepts in solid state chem. and electrochem. that have provided new opportunities for tailored design that can be extended to many different electrode materials for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqHBS0wIkomorVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgcpVUG7JFmRA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtVWmtL%252FE&amp;md5=023136cc0e5ed94e18ce0d526a0000a4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1149/1.1393348"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Stevens, D.                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Update on anode materials for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kang, Hongyan; Liu, Yongchang; Cao, Kangzhe; Zhao, Yan; Jiao, Lifang; Wang, Yijing; Yuan, Huatang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have emerged in recent years, due to their advantages of natural abundance, low cost and environmental friendliness.  In this article, we review the up-to-date research progress on anode materials for Na-ion batteries from five respects: carbon-based materials, alloy-based materials, metal oxides and sulfides based on conversion reaction, titanium-based compds. with insertion mechanism, and org. composites.  In particular, we not only summarize the Na-storage mechanism of these anodes, but also discuss the failure mechanism.  The problems and challenges assocd. with these anodes are pointed out.  Furthermore, on the basis of extensive reports and our exptl. studies, feasible strategies are suggested for designing high performance anode materials.  After further in-depth exploration and investigation, we believe that Na-ion batteries are promising alternative to lithium-ion batteries for low cost and large-scale energy storage systems in the near future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrB4Pf2vZ5QrrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgcpVUG7JFmRA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFelsrnN&amp;md5=8311789a2dc4e61dabff177245235c3e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1021/acs.accounts.5b00482"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shen, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bommier, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Na-Ion Battery Anodes: Materials and Electrochemistry</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Acc.                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-Ion Battery Anodes: Materials and Electrochemistry</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Wei; Shen, Fei; Bommier, Clement; Zhu, Hongli; Ji, Xiulei; Hu, Liangbing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Accounts of Chemical Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">49</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">231-240</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACHRE4</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The intermittent nature of renewable energy sources, such as solar and wind, calls for sustainable elec. energy storage (EES) technologies for stationary applications.  Li will be simply too rare for Li-ion batteries (LIBs) to be used for large-scale storage purposes.  In contrast, Na-ion batteries (NIBs) are highly promising to meet the demand of grid-level storage because Na is truly earth abundant and ubiquitous around the globe.  Furthermore, NIBs share a similar rocking-chair operation mechanism with LIBs, which potentially provides high reversibility and long cycling life.  It would be most efficient to transfer knowledge learned on LIBs during the last three decades to the development of NIBs.  Following this logic, rapid progress has been made in NIB cathode materials, where layered metal oxides and polyanionic compds. exhibit encouraging results.  On the anode side, pure graphite as the std. anode for LIBs can only form NaC64 in NIBs if solvent co-intercalation does not occur due to the unfavorable thermodn.  In fact, it was the utilization of a carbon anode in LIBs that enabled the com. successes.  Anodes of metal-ion batteries det. key characteristics, such as safety and cycling life; thus, it is indispensable to identify suitable anode materials for NIBs.In this Account, we review recent development on anode materials for NIBs.  Due to the limited space, we will mainly discuss carbon-based and alloy-based anodes and highlight progress made in our groups in this field.  We first present what is known about the failure mechanism of graphite anode in NIBs.  We then go on to discuss studies on hard carbon anodes, alloy-type anodes, and org. anodes.  Esp., the multiple functions of natural cellulose that is used as a low-cost carbon precursor for mass prodn. and as a soft substrate for tin anodes are highlighted.  The strategies of minimizing the surface area of carbon anodes for improving the first-cycle Coulombic efficiency are also outlined, where graphene oxide was employed as dehydration agent and 2,2,6,6-tetramethylpiperidine-1-oxyl (TEMPO) was used to unzip wood fiber.  Furthermore, surface modification by at. layer deposition technol. is introduced, where we discover that a thin layer of Al2O3 can function to encapsulate Sn nanoparticles, leading to a much enhanced cycling performance.  We also highlight recent work about the phosphorene/graphene anode, which outperformed other anodes in terms of capacity.  The arom. org. anode is also studied as anode with very high initial sodiation capacity.  Furthermore, electrochem. intercalation of Na ions into reduced graphene oxide is applied for fabricating transparent conductors, demonstrating the great feasibility of Na ion intercalation for optical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGorKnQvVSK3P7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lioFB9MFi8YHQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtVGksrg%253D&amp;md5=90d2907a2b33fdcf59913255073dd969</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1021/nl303305c"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Microstructural Evolution of Tin Nanoparticles during In Situ Sodium Insertion and Extraction</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Jiang Wei; Liu, Xiao Hua; Mao, Scott X.; Huang, Jian Yu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The microstructural changes and phase transformations of tin nanoparticles during electrochem. sodiation were studied with a nanosized sodium ion battery using in situ TEM.  The first sodiation process occurred in two steps; i.e., the cryst. Sn nanoparticles were initially sodiated via a two-phase mechanism with a migrating phase boundary to form a Na-poor, amorphous NaxSn alloy (x ∼ 0.5), which was further sodiated to several Na-rich amorphous phases and finally to the crystd. Na15Sn4 (x = 3.75) via a single-phase mechanism.  The volumetric expansion was ∼60% in the first step and 420% after the second step.  However, despite the huge expansion, cracking or fracture was not obsd., which is attributed to the second step of the single-phase sodiation that accommodates large portion of the sodiation-induced stress over the entire particle.  Excellent cyclability was also obsd. during the reversible sodiation/desodiation cycles, showing great potential of Sn nanoparticles as a robust electrode material for rechargeable batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq4-_RnLjqf7rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lioFB9MFi8YHQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhsFGqs7rO&amp;md5=3a9b283edadab9ac6dda7ef5c8bd18b7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201200346"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrochemical Performance of Porous Carbon/Tin Composite Anodes for Sodium-Ion and Lithium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemical performance of porous carbon/tin composite anodes for sodium-ion and lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Yunhua; Zhu, Yujie; Liu, Yihang; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. performance of mesoporous carbon (C)/tin (Sn) anodes in Na-ion and Li-ion batteries is systematically investigated.  The mesoporous C/Sn anodes in a Na-ion battery shows similar cycling stability but lower capacity and poorer rate capability than that in a Li-ion battery.  The desodiation potentials of Sn anodes are approx. 0.21 V lower than delithiation potentials.  The low capacity and poor rate capability of C/Sn anode in Na-ion batteries is mainly due to the large Na-ion size, resulting in slow Na-ion diffusion and large vol. change of porous C/Sn composite anode during alloy/dealloy reactions.  Understanding of the reaction mechanism between Sn and Na ions will provide insight towards exploring and designing new alloy-based anode materials for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqL8pwZXJa53LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lioFB9MFi8YHQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhsFKhtr8%253D&amp;md5=7fba4efb710816f1ca877f0494169a46</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1039/c2cc32730a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qian, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ai, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High Capacity Na-Storage and Superior Cyclability of Nanocomposite Sb/C Anode for Na-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have been proposed as candidates for replacing Li-ion batteries.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Conversion reactions for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Klein, Franziska; Jache, Birte; Bhide, Amrtha; Adelhelm, Philipp</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Chemistry Chemical Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Research on Na-ion batteries is focused on finding suitable electrode materials that enable cell reactions of high energy densities combined with low cost.  Naturally, an assessment of potential electrode materials requires a rational comparison with the analog reaction in Li-ion batteries.  The authors discuss the broad range of different conversion reactions for Na-ion batteries based on their basic thermodn. properties and compare them with their Li analogs.  Capacities, voltages, energy densities and vol. expansions are summarized to sketch out the scope for future studies in this research field.  For a given conversion electrode material, replacing Li by Na leads to a const. shift in cell potential ΔEo(Li-Na) depending on the material class.  For chlorides ΔEo(Li-Na) is nearly zero.  The theor. energy densities of conversion reactions of Na with fluorides or chlorides as pos. electrode materials typically reach values between 700 W h kg-1 and 1000 W h kg-1.  Next to the thermodn. assessment, results on several conversion reactions between Cu compds. (CuS, CuO, CuCl, CuCl2) and Na are being discussed.  Reactions with CuS and CuO were chosen because these compds. are frequently studied for conversion reactions with Li.  Chlorides are interesting because of ΔEo(Li-Na) ≈ 0 V As a result of chloride soly. in the electrolyte, the conversion process proceeds at defined potentials under rather small kinetic limitations.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpvFdD49Ctj47Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljqyv7QvLrt_g"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">3D-0D Graphene-Fe3O4 Quantum Dot Hybrids as High-Performance Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Huan; Jia, Mengqiu; Zhu, Qizhen; Cao, Bin; Chen, Renjie; Wang, Yu; Wu, Feng; Xu, Bin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">40</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">26878-26885</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal oxides can be considered as appealing candidates for sodium ion battery anode materials because these low-cost materials possess high capacity and enhanced safety.  However, the practical application of these materials is usually limited by their low electronic cond. and serious vol. change during the charging-discharging process.  Herein, we report the fabrication of 3D-0D graphene-Fe3O4 quantum dot hybrids by a facile one-pot hydrothermal approach as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  Fe3O4 quantum dots with an av. size of 4.9 nm are anchored on the surface of 3D structured graphene nanosheets homogeneously.  Such unique hierarchical structure are advantageous for enlarging the electrode/electrolyte interface area and enhancing the electrochem. activity of the hybrid materials, inhibiting particle aggregation of Fe3O4 and accommodating their vol. change during the charging-discharging process as well as enabling fast diffusion of electrons and rapid transfer of electrolyte ions.  Consequently, the 3D-0D graphene-Fe3O4 quantum dot hybrids exhibit ultrahigh sodium storage capacity (525 mAh/g at 30 mA/g), outstanding cycling stability (312 mAh/g after 200 cycles at 50 mA/g) and superior rate performance (56 mAh/g at 10 A/g).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqySiZNElc5Z7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgeePrzJ2QQBg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsFanu7rN&amp;md5=18e241446b270b8baeccc2c7fb9c0f0f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1039/c3cc40448j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Su, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ahn, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, G.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">SnO<sub>2</sub>@Graphene Nanocomposites as Anode Materials for Na-Ion Batteries with Superior Electrochemical Performance</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MnFe2O4@C Nanofibers as High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yongchang; Zhang, Ning; Yu, Chuanming; Jiao, Lifang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3321-3328</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">MnFe2O4 nanodots (∼3.3 nm) homogeneously dispersed in porous nitrogen-doped carbon nanofibers (denoted as MFO@C) were prepd. by a feasible electrospinning technique.  Meanwhile, MFO@C with the character of flexible free-standing membrane was directly used as binder- and current collector-free anode for sodium-ion batteries, exhibiting high electrochem. performance with high-rate capability (305 mA h g-1 at 10000 mA g-1 in comparison of 504 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1) and ultralong cycling life (ca. 90% capacity retention after 4200 cycles).  The Na-storage mechanism was systematically studied, revealing that MnFe2O4 is converted into metallic Mn and Fe after the first discharge (MnFe2O4 + 8Na+ + 8e- → Mn + 2Fe + 4Na2O) and then to MnO and Fe2O3 during the following charge (Mn + 2Fe + 4Na2O → MnO + Fe2O3 + 8Na+ + 8e-).  The subsequent cycles occur through reversible redox reactions of MnO + Fe2O3 + 8Na+ + 8e- &lt;-&gt; Mn + 2Fe + 4Na2O, of which the redn./oxidn. of MnO/Mn takes place at a lower potential than that of Fe2O3/Fe.  Furthermore, a soft package sodium-ion full battery with MFO@C anode and Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C cathode was assembled, delivering a stable capacity of ∼400 mA h g-1 for MFO@C (with 100 cycles at 500 mA g-1) and a promising energy d. of 77.8 Wh kg-1 for the whole battery.  This is owing to the distinctive structure of very-fine MnFe2O4 nanodots embedded in porous N-doped carbon nanofibers, which effectively improves the utilization rate of active materials, facilitates the transportation of electrons and Na+ ions, and prevents the particle pulverization/agglomeration upon prolonged cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo_fovS2KMexbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljEjKCH3JVD8g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XlsFKqtLk%253D&amp;md5=1f0fa2211d961158137c8cc4eb8fdd4c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201601329"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, S.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cobalt-Doped FeS2 Nanospheres with Complete Solid Solubility as a High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Kai; Park, Mihui; Zhou, Limin; Lee, Gi-Hyeok; Shin, Jeongyim; Hu, Zhe; Chou, Shu-Lei; Chen, Jun; Kang, Yong-Mook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Considering that the high capacity, long-term cycle life, and high-rate capability of anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) is a bottleneck currently, a series of Co-doped FeS2 solid solns. with different Co contents were prepd. by a facile solvothermal method, and for the first time their Na-storage properties were investigated. The redox reactions of NaxCo0.5Fe0.5S2 are dominated by pseudocapacitive behavior, leading to fast Na+ insertion/extn. and durable cycle life.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">FeSe2 Microspheres as a High-Performance Anode Material for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Kai; Hu, Zhe; Liu, Xue; Tao, Zhanliang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The use is demonstrated of FeSe2 as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries.  The FeSe2 microspheres assembled by nanooctahedra display a high tapping d. of 1.85 g cm-3 and a discharge capacity of 447 mA h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1.  The FeSe2 anode also exhibits long-term cyclic stability (372 mA h g-1 with capacity retention of 89.0% after 2000 cycles at 1 A g-1 ) and excellent high-rate performance 388 mA h g-1 at 10 C, 337 mA h g-1 at 20 C, 226 mA h g-1 at 50 C, where 1 C = 0.5 A g-1.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Urchin-Like CoSe2 as a High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Kai; Park, Mihui; Zhou, Limin; Lee, Gi-Hyeok; Li, Weijie; Kang, Yong-Mook; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">26</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">37</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6728-6735</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Urchin-like CoSe2 assembled by nanorods was synthesized via simple solvothermal route and was 1st applied as an anode material for Na-ion batteries (SIBs) with ether-based electrolytes.  The CoSe2 delivers excellent sodiation and de-sodiation properties when using 1 M NaCF3SO3 in diethyleneglycol dimethylether as an electrolyte and cycling between 0.5 and 3.0 V.  A high discharge capacity of 0.410 A h g-1 is obtained at 1 A g-1 after 1800 cycles, corresponding to a capacity retention of 98.6% calcd. from the 30th cycle.  Even at an ultrahigh rate of 50 A g-1, the capacity still maintains 0.097 A h g-1.  The reaction mechanism of the as-prepd. CoSe2 is also studied.  At discharged 1.56 V, insertion reaction occurs, while 2 conversion reactions take place at the 2nd and 3rd plateaus around 0.98 and 0.65 V.  During the charge process, Co 1st reacts with Na2Se to form NaxCoSe2 and then turns back to CoSe2.  In addn. to Na/CoSe2 half cells, Na3V2(PO4)3/CoSe2 full cell with excessive amt. of Na3V2(PO4)3 was studied.  The full cell exhibits a reversible capacity of 0.380 Ah g-1.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synergistic Na-Storage Reactions in Sn4P3 as a High-Capacity, Cycle-stable Anode of Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qian, Jiangfeng; Xiong, Ya; Cao, Yuliang; Ai, Xinping; Yang, Hanxi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Room-temp. Na-ion batteries have attracted great interest as a low cost and environmentally benign technol. for large scale elec. energy storage, however their development is hindered by the lack of suitable anodic host materials.  In this paper, a green approach is described for the synthesis of Sn4P3/C nanocomposite and demonstrated its excellent Na-storage performance as a novel anode of Na-ion batteries.  This Sn4P3/C anode can deliver a very high reversible capacity of 850 mA h g-1 with a remarkable rate capability with 50% capacity output at 500 mA g-1 and can also be cycled with 86% capacity retention over 150 cycles due to a synergistic Na-storage mechanism in the Sn4P3 anode, where the Sn nanoparticles act as electronic channels to enable electrochem. activation of the P component, while the elemental P and its sodiated product Na3P serve as a host matrix to alleviate the aggregation of the Sn particles during Na insertion reaction.  This mechanism may offer a new approach to create high capacity and cycle-stable alloy anodes for Na-ion batteries and other electrochem. energy storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrQCCVmbohfnbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh-khCP0-bRxw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXjvFSiurg%253D&amp;md5=1c703e0dccdc2b5cea071abf02396265</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1039/C3TA13976J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fullenwarth, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Darwiche, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Soares, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Donnadieu, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Monconduit, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">NiP<sub>3</sub>: a Promising Negative Electrode for Li- and Na-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">NiP3: a promising negative electrode for Li- and Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fullenwarth, J.; Darwiche, A.; Soares, A.; Donnadieu, B.; Monconduit, L.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to the abundance and low cost of sodium-contg. precursors ambient temp. sodium ion batteries are promising for large scale grid storage.  The low m.p. of Na (97.7 °C) compared to 180.6 °C for Li represents a significant safety hazard for the use of Na metal anodes at ambient temps., which emphasizes the need for scientists and engineers to identify, design and develop new neg. electrodes for Na-ion batteries.  The identification of a suitable neg. electrode is a crucial challenge for any further successful development of new cells, and to date efficient and competitive neg. electrodes for NaB are still very rare.  In this work we demonstrate that NiP3 could be a good challenger for this purpose.  NiP3 based electrodes are evaluated as neg. electrode materials for Li-ion batteries (LiB) and Na-ion batteries (NaB).  The study of the reaction mechanism reveals the formation of a phase of compn. close to Li3P and Na3P embedding Ni nanoparticles as the final reaction product after a full discharge.  While the direct conversion of NiP3 into Na3P is identified for the reaction vs. Na, it is still unclear whether an amorphous phase exists during the first discharge for the reaction vs. Li before the conversion.  Furthermore, thanks to the CM-cellulose/carbon black (CMC/CB) electrode formulation, the NiP3 electrode possesses a very promising capacity with a reversible storage capacity higher than 1000 mA h g-1 after 50 cycles for LiB and 900 mA h g-1 after 15 cycles for NaB, which represents one of the highest capacities ever sustained in Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpOUBqz1xXoSrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh-khCP0-bRxw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXpslGjug%253D%253D&amp;md5=1e5512e9a0282ca35cdf95497825a466</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1039/C3CC47977C"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jian, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zheng, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shi, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> Nanocrystals Anchored onto Graphene Nanosheets as the Anode Material for Low-Cost Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Towards more sustainable negative electrodes in Na-ion batteries via nanostructured iron oxide</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Valvo, M.; Lindgren, F.; Lafont, U.; Bjoerefors, F.; Edstroem, K.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">245</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion technol. could emerge as an alternative to Li-ion batteries due to limited costs and vast availability of sodium, as well as its similar chem.  Several Na-rich compds. were proposed as pos. electrodes, whereas suitable neg. counterparts were not found yet.  Nanostructured iron oxide is reported here for the 1st time as a potentially viable neg. electrode for Na-ion cells based on conventional electrolytes and composite coatings with CM-cellulose.  Electrochem. reactions of Na+ and Li+ ions with nanostructured Fe2O3 are analyzed and compared.  Initial sodiation of Fe2O3 yields a sloping profile in a voltage range characteristic for oxide conversion, which instead generates a typical plateau upon lithiation.  Application of such earth-abundant, nontoxic material in upcoming Na-ion batteries is potentially groundbreaking, since it offers important advantages, namely: i. simple and cost-effective synthesis of Fe2O3 nanostructures at low temps.; ii. cheaper and more sustainable cell fabrication with higher energy densities, e.g., use of natural, water-sol. binders, as well as Al for both current collectors; iii. electrochem. performances with specific gravimetric capacities exceeding 400 mAh g-1 at 40 mA g-1, accompanied by decent sp. vol. energy densities, e.g., ≈1.22 Wh cm-3, provided that cycle inefficiencies and long-term durability are addressed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoMUA0bO_kCk7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljMU7EhaJxRHA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Vacuum-annealing-tailored robust and flexible nanopore-structured γ-Fe2O3 film anodes for high capacity and long life Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Bai; Bao, Shu Juan; Le Xie, Jia; Li, Chang Ming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">69</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">36815-36820</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">RSCACL</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2046-2069</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Relatively high cost and limited resources are limiting the broad applications of Li-ion batteries.  Na-ion batteries are one of the most promising replacement candidates because of abundant sodium resources, low price and similarity with Li insertion chem.  For the first time, γ-Fe2O3 film was grown directly on a copper sheet with radio frequency magnetron sputtering as an anode for Na-ion batteries.  Results show that the γ-Fe2O3 film annealed at 600 °C delivers a high reversible capacity of 450 mA h g-1 and nearly 100% capacity retention over 100 charge-discharge cycles, significantly outperforming all the previously reported examples.  It is believed that the high performance of the Na-ion anode can be attributed to high temp. annealing producing nanopores for a large ion-inserting surface area and uniform γ-Fe2O3 particles firmly loaded on the surface of the Cu substrate to robustly retain the film structure during the Na-ion intercalation process for long cycle life.  This work holds great promise for the fabrication of inexpensive and non-toxic Na-ion batteries for practical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqfEwI227__J7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liqRd2pDVJjyw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXht1GhurnI&amp;md5=a9169b1bf2e94d1810fe5ef2a0ef51d4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA01334H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhong, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhong, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Z.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Subunits Controlled Synthesis of α-Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> Multi-Shelled Core–Shell Microspheres and Their Effects on Lithium/Sodium Ion Battery Performances</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Subunits controlled synthesis of α-Fe2O3 multi-shelled core-shell microspheres and their effects on lithium/sodium ion battery performances</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Zhen-guo; Zhong, Yan-jun; Liu, Jie; Wu, Jiao-hong; Guo, Xiao-dong; Zhong, Ben-he; Zhang, Zhi-ye</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Two kinds of Fe2O3 core-shell microspheres were synthesized.  The Fe2O3 sample obtained using ethanol (E-Fe2O3) contains a shell and a core assembled by nanoparticles with a diam. of ∼150 nm and the surface is fairly smooth.  Fe2O3 with optimized subunits was produced using water (W-Fe2O3).  The core is assembled by smaller nanoparticles of ∼50 nm.  The thicker shell and exterior surface possess porous nanorods.  These peculiar subunits endow W-Fe2O3 with a higher sp. surface area, more pore vol. and larger nanopores.  W-Fe2O3 displayed 733.1 mA-h/g at 6000 mA/g, which is more than two times that of E-Fe2O3 (306.5 mA-h/g).  Encouragingly, W-Fe2O3 also showed relatively promising sodium-ion battery performances.  The significantly different performances between E-Fe2O3 and W-Fe2O3 can be almost entirely attributed to their distinctive subunits.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rapid synthesis of α-Fe2O3/rGO nanocomposites by microwave autoclave as superior anodes for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Zhi-Jia; Wang, Yun-Xiao; Chou, Shu-Lei; Li, Hui-Jun; Liu, Hua-Kun; Wang, Jia-Zhao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">α-Fe2O3/reduced graphene oxide (rGO) nanocomposites were successfully synthesized within 15 min through a facile, environmentally friendly microwave hydrothermal method.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fe2O3-reduced graphene oxide composites synthesized via microwave-assisted method for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Xinjuan; Chen, Taiqiang; Chu, Haipeng; Niu, Lengyuan; Sun, Zhuo; Pan, Likun; Sun, Chang Q.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">166</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">12-16</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Fe2O3-reduced graphene oxide (RGO) composites were successfully fabricated via a facile microwave-assisted redn. of graphite oxide in Fe2O3 precursor soln. using a microwave system, and studied as anode material for Na ion batteries (SIBs).  Their morphologies, structures and electrochem. performance were characterized by TEM, x-ray diffraction, Raman spectroscopy, cyclic voltammetry and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy, resp.  The RGO addn. can enhance the electrochem. performance of Fe2O3-RGO composites.  Fe2O3-RGO composite with 30% RGO exhibits a max. reversible capacity of 289 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 50 mA g-1 after 50 cycles and excellent rate performance due to the synergistic effect between Fe2O3 and RGO.                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Seed-assisted growth of α-Fe2O3 nanorod arrays on reduced graphene oxide: a superior anode for high-performance Li-ion and Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kong, Dezhi; Cheng, Chuanwei; Wang, Ye; Liu, Bo; Huang, Zhixiang; Yang, Hui Ying</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">α-Fe2O3 nanorod/reduced graphene oxide nanosheet composites (denoted as α-Fe2O3@r-GO NRAs) are fabricated by using a facile and scalable seed-assisted hydrothermal growth route, in which the α-Fe2O3 nanorods are assembled onto the side surfaces of r-GO nanosheets.  Such α-Fe2O3@r-GO hybrid nanostructures are tested as anodes for both Li-ion and Na-ion batteries (LIBs and SIBs), which exhibit excellent performance with high capacity and long-cycling stability.  When used for LIBs, the hybrid α-Fe2O3@r-GO NRAs electrode exhibits a highly stable Li+ storage capacity of 1200 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles at 0.2C and excellent rate capability.  Moreover, the hybrid α-Fe2O3@r-GO NRAs also display their versatility as an anode for SIBs, which delivers high reversible Na+ storage capacity of 332 mA h g-1 at 0.2C over 300 cycles with long-term cycling stability.  The excellent electrochem. performance of the hybrid α-Fe2O3@r-GO NRAs anodes could be ascribed to the synergistic effect between the α-Fe2O3 nanorod arrays and reduced graphene oxide nanosheets, which could availably promote the charge transport and accommodate the vol. change upon the long-term charge-discharge process for reversible Li+ or Na+ storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp0a9WIAK0ChbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhbbr4pjr7XMw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtVynu7vF&amp;md5=9cc3cf3a07a3a6c7b5c62d4ce65ab67e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1002/adma.200800627"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wan, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nanostructured Materials for Electrochemical Energy Conversion and Storage Devices</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review of recent developments in nanostructured electrode materials for Li-ion batteries and fuel cell.  A challenge for the society is providing powerful electrochem. energy conversion and storage devices.  Rechargeable Li-ion batteries and fuel cells are promising candidates in terms of energy densities and power densities.  Nanostructured materials are of interest for such devices because of their high surface area, novel size effects and significantly enhanced kinetics.  The benefits of nanometer-size effects, the disadvantages of nanomaterials and strategies to solve these issues such as nano/micro hierarchical structures and surface coatings, as well as developments in the discovery of nanostructured Pt-based electrocatalysts for direct MeOH fuel cells are presented.  Approaches to lowering the cost of Pt catalysts include the use of (a) novel nanostructures of Pt, (b) new cost-effective synthesis routes, (c) binary or multiple catalysts, and (d) new catalyst supports.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqIhl84khqeSbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liYoyia_gIAGQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD1cXhtVCrs73L&amp;md5=17aabbed5996210ad96793fc61617851</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1016/S0167-2738(02)00061-9"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shi, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nano-Alloy Anode for Lithium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Solid State Ionics</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2002</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">148</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">247</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">258</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The features related to nano-alloy anode for Li-ion batteries are summarized in this paper mainly based on our recent studies on nano-SnSb.                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Investigation of the Electrode/Electrolyte Interface of Fe2O3 Composite Electrodes: Li vs Na Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Philippe, Bertrand; Valvo, Mario; Lindgren, Fredrik; Rensmo, Haakan; Edstroem, Kristina</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">26</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">17</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5028-5041</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We have investigated the properties of the electrode/electrolyte interfaces of composite electrodes based on nanostructured iron oxide cycled in Li- and Na-half cells contg. analogous electrolytes (i.e., LiClO4 or NaClO4 in ethylene carbonate:diethyl carbonate (EC:DEC)).  A meticulous nondestructive step-by-step anal. of the first discharge/charge cycle has been conducted via soft XPS using synchrotron radiation.  In this way, different depths were probed by varying the photon energy (hν) for both electrochem. systems.  The results of this thorough study clearly highlight the differences and the similarities of their resp. solid electrolyte interface (SEI) layers in terms of formation, compn., structure, or thickness, as well as their conversion mechanisms.  We specifically point out that the SEI coverage is more pronounced, and a homogeneous distribution rich in inorg. species exists in the case of Na, compared to the org./inorg. layered structure obsd. for the Li system.  The SEI formation gradually occurs during the first discharge in both Li- and Na-half cells.  For Na, a predeposit layer is formed directly by simple contact of the electrode with the electrolyte.  Despite using similar electrolytes, the nature of the cation (Li+ or Na+) has significant impact on the overall compn./structure of the resulting solid electrolyte interface (SEI).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrRCcAyoMEwYbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liYoyia_gIAGQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtlyms7nK&amp;md5=901217d73b4847de5186812a880f7095</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2015.03.151"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ding, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zheng, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pan, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tetragonal Hematite Single Crystals as Anode Materials for High Performance Lithium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tetragonal hematite single crystals as anode materials for high performance lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Shuanglei; Zhou, Banghong; Ding, Zhengping; Zheng, He; Huang, Lanping; Pan, Jun; Wu, Wei; Zhang, Hongbo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
